<s> each had come in from his night's amusement and pen was smoking his pipe and recounting as his habit was to his friend the observations and adventures of the evening just past <\s>
<s> how i am changed he said from the simpleton boy at fairoaks who was fit to break his heart about his first love <\s>
<s> lady mirabel had a reception to night and was as grave and collected as if she had been born a duchess and had never seen a trap door in her life <\s>
<s> and setting himself to work for what purposes will appear no doubt ulteriorly he soon had got a pretty accurate knowledge of lady clavering's affairs and fortune and of the prospects of her daughter and son <\s>
<s> the daughter was to have but a slender provision the bulk of the property was as before has been said to go to the son his father did not care for him or anybody else his mother was dotingly fond of him as the child of her latter days his sister disliked him <\s>
<s> such may be stated in round numbers to be the result of the information which major pendennis got <\s>
<s> my dear madam he would say patting the head of the boy this boy may wear a baron's coronet on his head on some future coronation if matters are but managed rightly and if sir francis clavering would but play his cards well <\s>
<s> at this the widow amory heaved a deep sigh <\s>
<s> he plays only much of his cards major i'm afraid she said <\s>
<s> the major owned that he knew as much did not disguise that he had heard of sir francis clavering's unfortunate propensity to play pitied lady clavering sincerely but spoke with such genuine sentiment and sense that her ladyship glad to find a person of experience to whom she could confide her grief and her condition talked about them pretty unreservedly to major pendennis and was eager to have his advice and consolation <\s>
<s> major pendennis became the begum's confidante and house friend and as a mother a wife and a capitalist she consulted him <\s>
<s> he gave her to understand showing at the same time a great deal of respectful sympathy that he was acquainted with some of the circumstances of her first unfortunate marriage and with even the person of her late husband whom he remembered in calcutta when she was living in seclusion with her father <\s>
<s> the poor lady with tears of shame more than of grief in her eyes told her version of her story <\s>
<s> going back a child to india after two years at a european school she had met amory and foolishly married him <\s>
<s> oh you don't know how miserable that man made me she said or what a life i passed betwixt him and my father <\s>
<s> before i saw him i had never seen a man except my father's clerks and native servants <\s>
<s> you know we didn't go into society in india on account of i know said major pendennis with a bow i was a wild romantic child my head was full of novels which i'd read at school i listened to his wild stories and adventures for he was a daring fellow and i thought he talked beautifully of those calm nights on the passage out when he used to <\s>
<s> well i married him and i was wretched from that day wretched with my father whose character you know major pendennis and i won't speak of but he wasn't a good man sir neither to my poor mother nor to me except that he left me his money nor to no one else that i ever heard of and he didn't do many kind actions in his lifetime i'm afraid <\s>
<s> and as for amory he was almost worse he was a spendthrift when my father was close he drank dreadfully and was furious when in that way <\s>
<s> he wasn't in any way a good or a faithful husband to me major pendennis and if he'd died in the gaol before this trial instead of afterwards he would have saved me a deal of shame and of unhappiness since sir <\s>
<s> lady clavering added for perhaps i should not have married at all if i had not been so anxious to change his horrid name and i have not been happy in my second husband as i suppose you know sir <\s>
<s> ah major pendennis i've got money to be sure and i'm a lady and people fancy i'm very happy but i ain't <\s>
<s> we all have our cares and griefs and troubles and many's the day that i sit down to one of my grand dinners with an aching heart and many a night do i lay awake on my fine bed a great deal more unhappy than the maid that makes for it <\s>
<s> i'm not a happy woman major for all the world says and envies the begum her diamonds and carriages and the great company that comes to my house <\s>
<s> i'm not happy in my husband i'm not in my daughter <\s>
<s> she ain't a good girl like that dear laura bell at fairoaks <\s>
<s> she's cost me many a tear though you don't see em and she sneers at her mother because i haven't had learning and that <\s>
<s> i was brought up amongst natives till i was twelve and went back to india when i was fourteen <\s>
<s> ah major i should have been a good woman if i had had a good husband <\s>
<s> and now i must go upstairs and wipe my eyes for they're red with cryin <\s>
<s> and lady rockminster's a comin and we're goin to ave a drive in the park <\s>
<s> and when lady rockminster made her appearance there was not a trace of tears or vexation on lady clavering's face but she was full of spirits and bounced out with her blunders and talk and murdered the king's english with the utmost liveliness and good humour <\s>
<s> begad she is not such a bad woman <\s>
<s> the major thought within himself <\s>
<s> she is not refined certainly and calls apollo apoller but she has some heart and i like that sort of thing and a devilish deal of money too <\s>
<s> three stars in india stock to her name begad <\s>
<s> which that young cub is to have is he <\s>
<s> and he thought how he should like to see a little of the money transferred to miss blanche and better still one of those stars shining in the name of mr <\s>
<s> still bent upon pursuing his schemes whatsoever they might be the old negotiator took the privilege of his intimacy and age to talk in a kindly and fatherly manner to miss blanche when he found occasion to see her alone <\s>
<s> he came in so frequently at luncheon time and became so familiar with the ladies that they did not even hesitate to quarrel before him and lady clavering whose tongue was loud and temper brusque had many a battle with the sylphide in the family friend's presence <\s>
<s> blanche's wit seldom failed to have the mastery in these encounters and the keen barbs of her arrows drove her adversary discomfited away <\s>
<s> i am an old fellow the major said i have nothing to do in life <\s>
<s> i have my eyes open <\s>
<s> i keep good counsel <\s>
<s> i am the friend of both of you and if you choose to quarrel before me why i shan't tell any one <\s>
<s> but you are two good people and i intend to make it up between you <\s>
<s> i have between lots of people husbands and wives fathers and sons daughters and mammas before this <\s>
<s> i like it i've nothing else to do <\s>
<s> one day then the old diplomatist entered lady clavering's drawing room just as the latter quitted it evidently in a high state of indignation and ran past him up the stairs to her own apartments <\s>
<s> she couldn't speak to him now she said she was a great deal too angry with that that that little wicked anger choked the rest of the words or prevented their utterance until lady clavering had passed out of hearing <\s>
<s> my dear good miss amory the major said entering the drawing room i see what is happening <\s>
<s> you and mamma have been disagreeing <\s>
<s> mothers and daughters disagree in the best families <\s>
<s> it was but last week that i healed up a quarrel between lady clapperton and her daughter lady claudia <\s>
<s> lady lear and her eldest daughter have not spoken for fourteen years <\s>
<s> kinder and more worthy people than these i never knew in the whole course of my life for everybody but each other admirable <\s>
<s> but they can't live together they oughtn't to live together and i wish my dear creature with all my soul that i could see you with an establishment of your own for there is no woman in london who could conduct one better with your own establishment making your own home happy <\s>
<s> i am not very happy in this one said the sylphide and the stupidity of mamma is enough to provoke a saint <\s>
<s> precisely so you are not suited to one another <\s>
<s> your mother committed one fault in early life or was it nature my dear in your case she ought not to have educated you <\s>
<s> you ought not to have been bred up to become the refined and intellectual being you are surrounded as i own you are by those who have not your genius or your refinement <\s>
<s> your place would be to lead in the most brilliant circles not to follow and take a second place in any society <\s>
<s> i have watched you miss amory you are ambitious and your proper sphere is command <\s>
<s> you ought to shine and you never can in this house i know it <\s>
<s> i hope i shall see you in another and a happier one some day and the mistress of it <\s>
<s> the sylphide shrugged her lily shoulders with a look of scorn <\s>
<s> where is the prince and where is the palace major pendennis <\s>
<s> but there is no romance in the world now no real affection <\s>
<s> no indeed said the major with the most sentimental and simple air which he could muster <\s>
<s> not that i know anything about it said blanche casting her eyes down except what i have read in novels <\s>
<s> of course not major pendennis cried how should you my dear young lady <\s>
<s> and novels ain't true as you remark admirably and there is no romance left in the world <\s>
<s> begad i wish i was a young fellow like my nephew <\s>
<s> and what continued miss amory musing what are the men whom we see about at the balls every night dancing guardsmen penniless treasury clerks boobies <\s>
<s> if i had my brother's fortune i might have such an establishment as you promise me but with my name and with my little means what am i to look to <\s>
<s> a country parson or a barrister in a street near russell square or a captain in a dragoon regiment who will take lodgings for me and come home from the mess tipsy and smelling of smoke like sir francis clavering <\s>
<s> that is how we girls are destined to end life <\s>
<s> o major pendennis i am sick of london and of balls and of young dandies with their chin tips and of the insolent great ladies who know us one day and cut us the next and of the world altogether <\s>
<s> i should like to leave it and to go into a convent that i should <\s>
<s> i shall never find anybody to understand me <\s>
<s> and i live here as much alone in my family and in the world as if i were in a cell locked up for ever <\s>
<s> i wish there were sisters of charity here and that i could be one and catch the plague and die of it i wish to quit the world <\s>
<s> i am not very old but i am tired i have suffered so much i've been so disillusionated i'm weary i'm weary o that the angel of death would come and beckon me away <\s>

<s> you know we didn't go into society in india on account of i know said major pendennis with a bow i was a wild romantic child my head was full of novels which i'd read at school i listened to his wild stories and adventures for he was a daring fellow and i thought he talked beautifully of those calm nights on the passage out when he used to <\s>
<s> well i married him and i was wretched from that day wretched with my father whose character you know major pendennis and i won't speak of but he wasn't a good man sir neither to my poor mother nor to me except that he left me his money nor to no one else that i ever heard of and he didn't do many kind actions in his lifetime i'm afraid <\s>
<s> and as for amory he was almost worse he was a spendthrift when my father was close he drank dreadfully and was furious when in that way <\s>
<s> he wasn't in any way a good or a faithful husband to me major pendennis and if he'd died in the gaol before this trial instead of afterwards he would have saved me a deal of shame and of unhappiness since sir <\s>
<s> lady clavering added for perhaps i should not have married at all if i had not been so anxious to change his horrid name and i have not been happy in my second husband as i suppose you know sir <\s>
<s> ah major pendennis i've got money to be sure and i'm a lady and people fancy i'm very happy but i ain't <\s>
<s> we all have our cares and griefs and troubles and many's the day that i sit down to one of my grand dinners with an aching heart and many a night do i lay awake on my fine bed a great deal more unhappy than the maid that makes for it <\s>
<s> i'm not a happy woman major for all the world says and envies the begum her diamonds and carriages and the great company that comes to my house <\s>
<s> i'm not happy in my husband i'm not in my daughter <\s>
<s> she ain't a good girl like that dear laura bell at fairoaks <\s>
<s> she's cost me many a tear though you don't see em and she sneers at her mother because i haven't had learning and that <\s>
<s> i was brought up amongst natives till i was twelve and went back to india when i was fourteen <\s>
<s> ah major i should have been a good woman if i had had a good husband <\s>
<s> and now i must go upstairs and wipe my eyes for they're red with cryin <\s>
<s> and lady rockminster's a comin and we're goin to ave a drive in the park <\s>
<s> and when lady rockminster made her appearance there was not a trace of tears or vexation on lady clavering's face but she was full of spirits and bounced out with her blunders and talk and murdered the king's english with the utmost liveliness and good humour <\s>
<s> begad she is not such a bad woman <\s>
<s> the major thought within himself <\s>

<s> and he thought how he should like to see a little of the money transferred to miss blanche and better still one of those stars shining in the name of mr <\s>
<s> still bent upon pursuing his schemes whatsoever they might be the old negotiator took the privilege of his intimacy and age to talk in a kindly and fatherly manner to miss blanche when he found occasion to see her alone <\s>
<s> he came in so frequently at luncheon time and became so familiar with the ladies that they did not even hesitate to quarrel before him and lady clavering whose tongue was loud and temper brusque had many a battle with the sylphide in the family friend's presence <\s>
<s> blanche's wit seldom failed to have the mastery in these encounters and the keen barbs of her arrows drove her adversary discomfited away <\s>
<s> i am an old fellow the major said i have nothing to do in life <\s>
<s> i have my eyes open <\s>
<s> i keep good counsel <\s>

<s> i like it i've nothing else to do <\s>
<s> one day then the old diplomatist entered lady clavering's drawing room just as the latter quitted it evidently in a high state of indignation and ran past him up the stairs to her own apartments <\s>
<s> she couldn't speak to him now she said she was a great deal too angry with that that that little wicked anger choked the rest of the words or prevented their utterance until lady clavering had passed out of hearing <\s>
<s> my dear good miss amory the major said entering the drawing room i see what is happening <\s>
<s> you and mamma have been disagreeing <\s>
<s> mothers and daughters disagree in the best families <\s>
<s> it was but last week that i healed up a quarrel between lady clapperton and her daughter lady claudia <\s>
<s> lady lear and her eldest daughter have not spoken for fourteen years <\s>
<s> kinder and more worthy people than these i never knew in the whole course of my life for everybody but each other admirable <\s>
<s> but they can't live together they oughtn't to live together and i wish my dear creature with all my soul that i could see you with an establishment of your own for there is no woman in london who could conduct one better with your own establishment making your own home happy <\s>
<s> i am not very happy in this one said the sylphide and the stupidity of mamma is enough to provoke a saint <\s>
<s> precisely so you are not suited to one another <\s>
<s> your mother committed one fault in early life or was it nature my dear in your case she ought not to have educated you <\s>
<s> you ought not to have been bred up to become the refined and intellectual being you are surrounded as i own you are by those who have not your genius or your refinement <\s>
<s> your place would be to lead in the most brilliant circles not to follow and take a second place in any society <\s>
<s> i have watched you miss amory you are ambitious and your proper sphere is command <\s>
<s> you ought to shine and you never can in this house i know it <\s>
<s> i hope i shall see you in another and a happier one some day and the mistress of it <\s>
<s> the sylphide shrugged her lily shoulders with a look of scorn <\s>
<s> where is the prince and where is the palace major pendennis <\s>
<s> but there is no romance in the world now no real affection <\s>
<s> no indeed said the major with the most sentimental and simple air which he could muster <\s>

<s> and novels ain't true as you remark admirably and there is no romance left in the world <\s>
<s> begad i wish i was a young fellow like my nephew <\s>
<s> and what continued miss amory musing what are the men whom we see about at the balls every night dancing guardsmen penniless treasury clerks boobies <\s>
<s> if i had my brother's fortune i might have such an establishment as you promise me but with my name and with my little means what am i to look to <\s>
<s> a country parson or a barrister in a street near russell square or a captain in a dragoon regiment who will take lodgings for me and come home from the mess tipsy and smelling of smoke like sir francis clavering <\s>
<s> that is how we girls are destined to end life <\s>
<s> o major pendennis i am sick of london and of balls and of young dandies with their chin tips and of the insolent great ladies who know us one day and cut us the next and of the world altogether <\s>
<s> i should like to leave it and to go into a convent that i should <\s>
<s> i shall never find anybody to understand me <\s>
<s> and i live here as much alone in my family and in the world as if i were in a cell locked up for ever <\s>
<s> i wish there were sisters of charity here and that i could be one and catch the plague and die of it i wish to quit the world <\s>
<s> i am not very old but i am tired i have suffered so much i've been so disillusionated i'm weary i'm weary o that the angel of death would come and beckon me away <\s>

<s> the prince don't marry nowadays as you say unless the princess has a doosid deal of money in the funds or is a lady of his own rank the young folks of the great families marry into the great families if they haven't fortune they have each other's shoulders to push on in the world which is pretty nearly as good a girl with your fortune can scarcely hope for a great match but a girl with your genius and your admirable tact and fine manners with a clever husband by her side may make any place for herself in the world we are grown doosid republican <\s>

<s> this speech may be interpreted as follows <\s>

<s> the major owned that he knew as much did not disguise that he had heard of sir francis clavering's unfortunate propensity to play pitied lady clavering sincerely but spoke with such genuine sentiment and sense that her ladyship glad to find a person of experience to whom she could confide her grief and her condition talked about them pretty unreservedly to major pendennis and was eager to have his advice and consolation <\s>
<s> major pendennis became the begum's confidante and house friend and as a mother a wife and a capitalist she consulted him <\s>

<s> where is the prince and where is the palace major pendennis <\s>
<s> but there is no romance in the world now no real affection <\s>
<s> no indeed said the major with the most sentimental and simple air which he could muster <\s>
<s> not that i know anything about it said blanche casting her eyes down except what i have read in novels <\s>
<s> of course not major pendennis cried how should you my dear young lady <\s>
<s> and novels ain't true as you remark admirably and there is no romance left in the world <\s>
<s> begad i wish i was a young fellow like my nephew <\s>
<s> and what continued miss amory musing what are the men whom we see about at the balls every night dancing guardsmen penniless treasury clerks boobies <\s>
<s> if i had my brother's fortune i might have such an establishment as you promise me but with my name and with my little means what am i to look to <\s>
<s> a country parson or a barrister in a street near russell square or a captain in a dragoon regiment who will take lodgings for me and come home from the mess tipsy and smelling of smoke like sir francis clavering <\s>
<s> that is how we girls are destined to end life <\s>
<s> o major pendennis i am sick of london and of balls and of young dandies with their chin tips and of the insolent great ladies who know us one day and cut us the next and of the world altogether <\s>
<s> i should like to leave it and to go into a convent that i should <\s>
<s> i shall never find anybody to understand me <\s>
<s> and i live here as much alone in my family and in the world as if i were in a cell locked up for ever <\s>
<s> i wish there were sisters of charity here and that i could be one and catch the plague and die of it i wish to quit the world <\s>
<s> i am not very old but i am tired i have suffered so much i've been so disillusionated i'm weary i'm weary o that the angel of death would come and beckon me away <\s>
<s> this speech may be interpreted as follows <\s>
<s> a few nights since a great lady lady flamingo had cut miss amory and lady clavering <\s>
<s> she was quite mad because she could not get an invitation to lady drum's ball it was the end of the season and nobody had proposed to her she had made no sensation at all she who was so much cleverer than any girl of the year and of the young ladies forming her special circle <\s>
<s> dora who had but five thousand pounds flora who had nothing and leonora who had red hair were going to be married and nobody had come for blanche amory <\s>
<s> you judge wisely about the world and about your position my dear miss blanche the major said <\s>
<s> the prince don't marry nowadays as you say unless the princess has a doosid deal of money in the funds or is a lady of his own rank the young folks of the great families marry into the great families if they haven't fortune they have each other's shoulders to push on in the world which is pretty nearly as good a girl with your fortune can scarcely hope for a great match but a girl with your genius and your admirable tact and fine manners with a clever husband by her side may make any place for herself in the world we are grown doosid republican <\s>
<s> talent ranks with birth and wealth now begad and a clever man with a clever wife may take any place they please <\s>
<s> miss amory did not of course in the least understand what major pendennis meant perhaps she thought over circumstances in her mind and asked herself could he be a negotiator for a former suitor of hers and could he mean pen <\s>
<s> no it was impossible he had been civil but nothing more so she said laughing who is the clever man and when will you bring him to me major pendennis <\s>
<s> i am dying to see him <\s>

<s> henry foker at which name and at the appearance of our friend both the lady and the gentleman burst out laughing <\s>
<s> that is not the man major pendennis said <\s>
<s> he is engaged to his cousin lord gravesend's daughter good bye my dear miss amory <\s>
<s> was pen growing worldly and should a man not get the experience of the world and lay it to his account <\s>
<s> he felt for his part as he said that he was growing very old very soon <\s>
<s> how this town forms and changes us he said once to warrington <\s>
<s> each had come in from his night's amusement and pen was smoking his pipe and recounting as his habit was to his friend the observations and adventures of the evening just past <\s>
<s> how i am changed he said from the simpleton boy at fairoaks who was fit to break his heart about his first love <\s>
<s> lady mirabel had a reception to night and was as grave and collected as if she had been born a duchess and had never seen a trap door in her life <\s>
<s> and setting himself to work for what purposes will appear no doubt ulteriorly he soon had got a pretty accurate knowledge of lady clavering's affairs and fortune and of the prospects of her daughter and son <\s>
<s> the daughter was to have but a slender provision the bulk of the property was as before has been said to go to the son his father did not care for him or anybody else his mother was dotingly fond of him as the child of her latter days his sister disliked him <\s>
<s> such may be stated in round numbers to be the result of the information which major pendennis got <\s>
<s> my dear madam he would say patting the head of the boy this boy may wear a baron's coronet on his head on some future coronation if matters are but managed rightly and if sir francis clavering would but play his cards well <\s>
<s> at this the widow amory heaved a deep sigh <\s>
<s> he plays only much of his cards major i'm afraid she said <\s>
<s> the major owned that he knew as much did not disguise that he had heard of sir francis clavering's unfortunate propensity to play pitied lady clavering sincerely but spoke with such genuine sentiment and sense that her ladyship glad to find a person of experience to whom she could confide her grief and her condition talked about them pretty unreservedly to major pendennis and was eager to have his advice and consolation <\s>
<s> major pendennis became the begum's confidante and house friend and as a mother a wife and a capitalist she consulted him <\s>
<s> he gave her to understand showing at the same time a great deal of respectful sympathy that he was acquainted with some of the circumstances of her first unfortunate marriage and with even the person of her late husband whom he remembered in calcutta when she was living in seclusion with her father <\s>
<s> the poor lady with tears of shame more than of grief in her eyes told her version of her story <\s>
<s> going back a child to india after two years at a european school she had met amory and foolishly married him <\s>
<s> oh you don't know how miserable that man made me she said or what a life i passed betwixt him and my father <\s>
<s> before i saw him i had never seen a man except my father's clerks and native servants <\s>
<s> you know we didn't go into society in india on account of i know said major pendennis with a bow i was a wild romantic child my head was full of novels which i'd read at school i listened to his wild stories and adventures for he was a daring fellow and i thought he talked beautifully of those calm nights on the passage out when he used to <\s>
<s> well i married him and i was wretched from that day wretched with my father whose character you know major pendennis and i won't speak of but he wasn't a good man sir neither to my poor mother nor to me except that he left me his money nor to no one else that i ever heard of and he didn't do many kind actions in his lifetime i'm afraid <\s>
<s> and as for amory he was almost worse he was a spendthrift when my father was close he drank dreadfully and was furious when in that way <\s>
<s> he wasn't in any way a good or a faithful husband to me major pendennis and if he'd died in the gaol before this trial instead of afterwards he would have saved me a deal of shame and of unhappiness since sir <\s>
<s> lady clavering added for perhaps i should not have married at all if i had not been so anxious to change his horrid name and i have not been happy in my second husband as i suppose you know sir <\s>
<s> ah major pendennis i've got money to be sure and i'm a lady and people fancy i'm very happy but i ain't <\s>
<s> we all have our cares and griefs and troubles and many's the day that i sit down to one of my grand dinners with an aching heart and many a night do i lay awake on my fine bed a great deal more unhappy than the maid that makes for it <\s>
<s> i'm not a happy woman major for all the world says and envies the begum her diamonds and carriages and the great company that comes to my house <\s>
<s> i'm not happy in my husband i'm not in my daughter <\s>
<s> she ain't a good girl like that dear laura bell at fairoaks <\s>
<s> she's cost me many a tear though you don't see em and she sneers at her mother because i haven't had learning and that <\s>
<s> i was brought up amongst natives till i was twelve and went back to india when i was fourteen <\s>
<s> ah major i should have been a good woman if i had had a good husband <\s>
<s> and now i must go upstairs and wipe my eyes for they're red with cryin <\s>
<s> and lady rockminster's a comin and we're goin to ave a drive in the park <\s>
<s> and when lady rockminster made her appearance there was not a trace of tears or vexation on lady clavering's face but she was full of spirits and bounced out with her blunders and talk and murdered the king's english with the utmost liveliness and good humour <\s>
<s> begad she is not such a bad woman <\s>
<s> the major thought within himself <\s>
<s> she is not refined certainly and calls apollo apoller but she has some heart and i like that sort of thing and a devilish deal of money too <\s>

<s> miss amory did not of course in the least understand what major pendennis meant perhaps she thought over circumstances in her mind and asked herself could he be a negotiator for a former suitor of hers and could he mean pen <\s>

<s> each had come in from his night's amusement and pen was smoking his pipe and recounting as his habit was to his friend the observations and adventures of the evening just past <\s>
<s> how i am changed he said from the simpleton boy at fairoaks who was fit to break his heart about his first love <\s>
<s> lady mirabel had a reception to night and was as grave and collected as if she had been born a duchess and had never seen a trap door in her life <\s>
<s> and setting himself to work for what purposes will appear no doubt ulteriorly he soon had got a pretty accurate knowledge of lady clavering's affairs and fortune and of the prospects of her daughter and son <\s>
<s> the daughter was to have but a slender provision the bulk of the property was as before has been said to go to the son his father did not care for him or anybody else his mother was dotingly fond of him as the child of her latter days his sister disliked him <\s>
<s> such may be stated in round numbers to be the result of the information which major pendennis got <\s>
<s> my dear madam he would say patting the head of the boy this boy may wear a baron's coronet on his head on some future coronation if matters are but managed rightly and if sir francis clavering would but play his cards well <\s>
<s> at this the widow amory heaved a deep sigh <\s>
<s> he plays only much of his cards major i'm afraid she said <\s>
<s> the major owned that he knew as much did not disguise that he had heard of sir francis clavering's unfortunate propensity to play pitied lady clavering sincerely but spoke with such genuine sentiment and sense that her ladyship glad to find a person of experience to whom she could confide her grief and her condition talked about them pretty unreservedly to major pendennis and was eager to have his advice and consolation <\s>
<s> major pendennis became the begum's confidante and house friend and as a mother a wife and a capitalist she consulted him <\s>
<s> he gave her to understand showing at the same time a great deal of respectful sympathy that he was acquainted with some of the circumstances of her first unfortunate marriage and with even the person of her late husband whom he remembered in calcutta when she was living in seclusion with her father <\s>
<s> the poor lady with tears of shame more than of grief in her eyes told her version of her story <\s>
<s> going back a child to india after two years at a european school she had met amory and foolishly married him <\s>
<s> oh you don't know how miserable that man made me she said or what a life i passed betwixt him and my father <\s>
<s> before i saw him i had never seen a man except my father's clerks and native servants <\s>
<s> you know we didn't go into society in india on account of i know said major pendennis with a bow i was a wild romantic child my head was full of novels which i'd read at school i listened to his wild stories and adventures for he was a daring fellow and i thought he talked beautifully of those calm nights on the passage out when he used to <\s>
<s> well i married him and i was wretched from that day wretched with my father whose character you know major pendennis and i won't speak of but he wasn't a good man sir neither to my poor mother nor to me except that he left me his money nor to no one else that i ever heard of and he didn't do many kind actions in his lifetime i'm afraid <\s>
<s> and as for amory he was almost worse he was a spendthrift when my father was close he drank dreadfully and was furious when in that way <\s>
<s> he wasn't in any way a good or a faithful husband to me major pendennis and if he'd died in the gaol before this trial instead of afterwards he would have saved me a deal of shame and of unhappiness since sir <\s>
<s> lady clavering added for perhaps i should not have married at all if i had not been so anxious to change his horrid name and i have not been happy in my second husband as i suppose you know sir <\s>
<s> ah major pendennis i've got money to be sure and i'm a lady and people fancy i'm very happy but i ain't <\s>
<s> we all have our cares and griefs and troubles and many's the day that i sit down to one of my grand dinners with an aching heart and many a night do i lay awake on my fine bed a great deal more unhappy than the maid that makes for it <\s>
<s> i'm not a happy woman major for all the world says and envies the begum her diamonds and carriages and the great company that comes to my house <\s>
<s> i'm not happy in my husband i'm not in my daughter <\s>
<s> she ain't a good girl like that dear laura bell at fairoaks <\s>
<s> she's cost me many a tear though you don't see em and she sneers at her mother because i haven't had learning and that <\s>
<s> i was brought up amongst natives till i was twelve and went back to india when i was fourteen <\s>
<s> ah major i should have been a good woman if i had had a good husband <\s>
<s> and now i must go upstairs and wipe my eyes for they're red with cryin <\s>
<s> and lady rockminster's a comin and we're goin to ave a drive in the park <\s>
<s> and when lady rockminster made her appearance there was not a trace of tears or vexation on lady clavering's face but she was full of spirits and bounced out with her blunders and talk and murdered the king's english with the utmost liveliness and good humour <\s>
<s> begad she is not such a bad woman <\s>
<s> the major thought within himself <\s>
<s> she is not refined certainly and calls apollo apoller but she has some heart and i like that sort of thing and a devilish deal of money too <\s>
<s> three stars in india stock to her name begad <\s>
<s> which that young cub is to have is he <\s>
<s> and he thought how he should like to see a little of the money transferred to miss blanche and better still one of those stars shining in the name of mr <\s>
<s> still bent upon pursuing his schemes whatsoever they might be the old negotiator took the privilege of his intimacy and age to talk in a kindly and fatherly manner to miss blanche when he found occasion to see her alone <\s>
<s> he came in so frequently at luncheon time and became so familiar with the ladies that they did not even hesitate to quarrel before him and lady clavering whose tongue was loud and temper brusque had many a battle with the sylphide in the family friend's presence <\s>
<s> blanche's wit seldom failed to have the mastery in these encounters and the keen barbs of her arrows drove her adversary discomfited away <\s>
<s> i am an old fellow the major said i have nothing to do in life <\s>
<s> i have my eyes open <\s>
<s> i keep good counsel <\s>
<s> i am the friend of both of you and if you choose to quarrel before me why i shan't tell any one <\s>
<s> but you are two good people and i intend to make it up between you <\s>
<s> i have between lots of people husbands and wives fathers and sons daughters and mammas before this <\s>
<s> i like it i've nothing else to do <\s>
<s> one day then the old diplomatist entered lady clavering's drawing room just as the latter quitted it evidently in a high state of indignation and ran past him up the stairs to her own apartments <\s>
<s> she couldn't speak to him now she said she was a great deal too angry with that that that little wicked anger choked the rest of the words or prevented their utterance until lady clavering had passed out of hearing <\s>
<s> my dear good miss amory the major said entering the drawing room i see what is happening <\s>
<s> you and mamma have been disagreeing <\s>
<s> mothers and daughters disagree in the best families <\s>
<s> it was but last week that i healed up a quarrel between lady clapperton and her daughter lady claudia <\s>
<s> lady lear and her eldest daughter have not spoken for fourteen years <\s>
<s> kinder and more worthy people than these i never knew in the whole course of my life for everybody but each other admirable <\s>
<s> but they can't live together they oughtn't to live together and i wish my dear creature with all my soul that i could see you with an establishment of your own for there is no woman in london who could conduct one better with your own establishment making your own home happy <\s>
<s> i am not very happy in this one said the sylphide and the stupidity of mamma is enough to provoke a saint <\s>
<s> precisely so you are not suited to one another <\s>
<s> your mother committed one fault in early life or was it nature my dear in your case she ought not to have educated you <\s>
<s> you ought not to have been bred up to become the refined and intellectual being you are surrounded as i own you are by those who have not your genius or your refinement <\s>
<s> your place would be to lead in the most brilliant circles not to follow and take a second place in any society <\s>
<s> i have watched you miss amory you are ambitious and your proper sphere is command <\s>
<s> you ought to shine and you never can in this house i know it <\s>
<s> i hope i shall see you in another and a happier one some day and the mistress of it <\s>

<s> where is the prince and where is the palace major pendennis <\s>

<s> he gave her to understand showing at the same time a great deal of respectful sympathy that he was acquainted with some of the circumstances of her first unfortunate marriage and with even the person of her late husband whom he remembered in calcutta when she was living in seclusion with her father <\s>
<s> the poor lady with tears of shame more than of grief in her eyes told her version of her story <\s>
<s> going back a child to india after two years at a european school she had met amory and foolishly married him <\s>
<s> oh you don't know how miserable that man made me she said or what a life i passed betwixt him and my father <\s>
<s> before i saw him i had never seen a man except my father's clerks and native servants <\s>
<s> you know we didn't go into society in india on account of i know said major pendennis with a bow i was a wild romantic child my head was full of novels which i'd read at school i listened to his wild stories and adventures for he was a daring fellow and i thought he talked beautifully of those calm nights on the passage out when he used to <\s>
<s> well i married him and i was wretched from that day wretched with my father whose character you know major pendennis and i won't speak of but he wasn't a good man sir neither to my poor mother nor to me except that he left me his money nor to no one else that i ever heard of and he didn't do many kind actions in his lifetime i'm afraid <\s>
<s> and as for amory he was almost worse he was a spendthrift when my father was close he drank dreadfully and was furious when in that way <\s>
<s> he wasn't in any way a good or a faithful husband to me major pendennis and if he'd died in the gaol before this trial instead of afterwards he would have saved me a deal of shame and of unhappiness since sir <\s>
<s> lady clavering added for perhaps i should not have married at all if i had not been so anxious to change his horrid name and i have not been happy in my second husband as i suppose you know sir <\s>
<s> ah major pendennis i've got money to be sure and i'm a lady and people fancy i'm very happy but i ain't <\s>
<s> we all have our cares and griefs and troubles and many's the day that i sit down to one of my grand dinners with an aching heart and many a night do i lay awake on my fine bed a great deal more unhappy than the maid that makes for it <\s>
<s> i'm not a happy woman major for all the world says and envies the begum her diamonds and carriages and the great company that comes to my house <\s>
<s> i'm not happy in my husband i'm not in my daughter <\s>
<s> she ain't a good girl like that dear laura bell at fairoaks <\s>
<s> she's cost me many a tear though you don't see em and she sneers at her mother because i haven't had learning and that <\s>
<s> i was brought up amongst natives till i was twelve and went back to india when i was fourteen <\s>
<s> ah major i should have been a good woman if i had had a good husband <\s>
<s> and now i must go upstairs and wipe my eyes for they're red with cryin <\s>
<s> and lady rockminster's a comin and we're goin to ave a drive in the park <\s>
<s> and when lady rockminster made her appearance there was not a trace of tears or vexation on lady clavering's face but she was full of spirits and bounced out with her blunders and talk and murdered the king's english with the utmost liveliness and good humour <\s>
<s> begad she is not such a bad woman <\s>
<s> the major thought within himself <\s>
<s> she is not refined certainly and calls apollo apoller but she has some heart and i like that sort of thing and a devilish deal of money too <\s>
<s> three stars in india stock to her name begad <\s>
<s> which that young cub is to have is he <\s>
<s> and he thought how he should like to see a little of the money transferred to miss blanche and better still one of those stars shining in the name of mr <\s>
<s> still bent upon pursuing his schemes whatsoever they might be the old negotiator took the privilege of his intimacy and age to talk in a kindly and fatherly manner to miss blanche when he found occasion to see her alone <\s>
<s> he came in so frequently at luncheon time and became so familiar with the ladies that they did not even hesitate to quarrel before him and lady clavering whose tongue was loud and temper brusque had many a battle with the sylphide in the family friend's presence <\s>
<s> blanche's wit seldom failed to have the mastery in these encounters and the keen barbs of her arrows drove her adversary discomfited away <\s>
<s> i am an old fellow the major said i have nothing to do in life <\s>
<s> i have my eyes open <\s>
<s> i keep good counsel <\s>
<s> i am the friend of both of you and if you choose to quarrel before me why i shan't tell any one <\s>
<s> but you are two good people and i intend to make it up between you <\s>
<s> i have between lots of people husbands and wives fathers and sons daughters and mammas before this <\s>
<s> i like it i've nothing else to do <\s>
<s> one day then the old diplomatist entered lady clavering's drawing room just as the latter quitted it evidently in a high state of indignation and ran past him up the stairs to her own apartments <\s>
<s> she couldn't speak to him now she said she was a great deal too angry with that that that little wicked anger choked the rest of the words or prevented their utterance until lady clavering had passed out of hearing <\s>
<s> my dear good miss amory the major said entering the drawing room i see what is happening <\s>
<s> you and mamma have been disagreeing <\s>
<s> mothers and daughters disagree in the best families <\s>
<s> it was but last week that i healed up a quarrel between lady clapperton and her daughter lady claudia <\s>
<s> lady lear and her eldest daughter have not spoken for fourteen years <\s>
<s> kinder and more worthy people than these i never knew in the whole course of my life for everybody but each other admirable <\s>
<s> but they can't live together they oughtn't to live together and i wish my dear creature with all my soul that i could see you with an establishment of your own for there is no woman in london who could conduct one better with your own establishment making your own home happy <\s>
<s> i am not very happy in this one said the sylphide and the stupidity of mamma is enough to provoke a saint <\s>
<s> precisely so you are not suited to one another <\s>
<s> your mother committed one fault in early life or was it nature my dear in your case she ought not to have educated you <\s>
<s> you ought not to have been bred up to become the refined and intellectual being you are surrounded as i own you are by those who have not your genius or your refinement <\s>
<s> your place would be to lead in the most brilliant circles not to follow and take a second place in any society <\s>
<s> i have watched you miss amory you are ambitious and your proper sphere is command <\s>
<s> you ought to shine and you never can in this house i know it <\s>
<s> i hope i shall see you in another and a happier one some day and the mistress of it <\s>
<s> the sylphide shrugged her lily shoulders with a look of scorn <\s>
<s> where is the prince and where is the palace major pendennis <\s>
<s> but there is no romance in the world now no real affection <\s>
<s> no indeed said the major with the most sentimental and simple air which he could muster <\s>
<s> not that i know anything about it said blanche casting her eyes down except what i have read in novels <\s>
<s> of course not major pendennis cried how should you my dear young lady <\s>
<s> and novels ain't true as you remark admirably and there is no romance left in the world <\s>
<s> begad i wish i was a young fellow like my nephew <\s>
<s> and what continued miss amory musing what are the men whom we see about at the balls every night dancing guardsmen penniless treasury clerks boobies <\s>
<s> if i had my brother's fortune i might have such an establishment as you promise me but with my name and with my little means what am i to look to <\s>
<s> a country parson or a barrister in a street near russell square or a captain in a dragoon regiment who will take lodgings for me and come home from the mess tipsy and smelling of smoke like sir francis clavering <\s>
<s> that is how we girls are destined to end life <\s>
<s> o major pendennis i am sick of london and of balls and of young dandies with their chin tips and of the insolent great ladies who know us one day and cut us the next and of the world altogether <\s>
<s> i should like to leave it and to go into a convent that i should <\s>
<s> i shall never find anybody to understand me <\s>
<s> and i live here as much alone in my family and in the world as if i were in a cell locked up for ever <\s>
<s> i wish there were sisters of charity here and that i could be one and catch the plague and die of it i wish to quit the world <\s>
<s> i am not very old but i am tired i have suffered so much i've been so disillusionated i'm weary i'm weary o that the angel of death would come and beckon me away <\s>
<s> this speech may be interpreted as follows <\s>
<s> a few nights since a great lady lady flamingo had cut miss amory and lady clavering <\s>
<s> she was quite mad because she could not get an invitation to lady drum's ball it was the end of the season and nobody had proposed to her she had made no sensation at all she who was so much cleverer than any girl of the year and of the young ladies forming her special circle <\s>
<s> dora who had but five thousand pounds flora who had nothing and leonora who had red hair were going to be married and nobody had come for blanche amory <\s>
<s> you judge wisely about the world and about your position my dear miss blanche the major said <\s>
<s> the prince don't marry nowadays as you say unless the princess has a doosid deal of money in the funds or is a lady of his own rank the young folks of the great families marry into the great families if they haven't fortune they have each other's shoulders to push on in the world which is pretty nearly as good a girl with your fortune can scarcely hope for a great match but a girl with your genius and your admirable tact and fine manners with a clever husband by her side may make any place for herself in the world we are grown doosid republican <\s>
<s> talent ranks with birth and wealth now begad and a clever man with a clever wife may take any place they please <\s>

<s> i am not very happy in this one said the sylphide and the stupidity of mamma is enough to provoke a saint <\s>

<s> your mother committed one fault in early life or was it nature my dear in your case she ought not to have educated you <\s>

<s> that is how we girls are destined to end life <\s>
<s> o major pendennis i am sick of london and of balls and of young dandies with their chin tips and of the insolent great ladies who know us one day and cut us the next and of the world altogether <\s>
<s> i should like to leave it and to go into a convent that i should <\s>
<s> i shall never find anybody to understand me <\s>
<s> and i live here as much alone in my family and in the world as if i were in a cell locked up for ever <\s>

<s> i am not very old but i am tired i have suffered so much i've been so disillusionated i'm weary i'm weary o that the angel of death would come and beckon me away <\s>
<s> this speech may be interpreted as follows <\s>

<s> the prince don't marry nowadays as you say unless the princess has a doosid deal of money in the funds or is a lady of his own rank the young folks of the great families marry into the great families if they haven't fortune they have each other's shoulders to push on in the world which is pretty nearly as good a girl with your fortune can scarcely hope for a great match but a girl with your genius and your admirable tact and fine manners with a clever husband by her side may make any place for herself in the world we are grown doosid republican <\s>
<s> talent ranks with birth and wealth now begad and a clever man with a clever wife may take any place they please <\s>

<s> precisely so you are not suited to one another <\s>
<s> your mother committed one fault in early life or was it nature my dear in your case she ought not to have educated you <\s>
<s> you ought not to have been bred up to become the refined and intellectual being you are surrounded as i own you are by those who have not your genius or your refinement <\s>
<s> your place would be to lead in the most brilliant circles not to follow and take a second place in any society <\s>
<s> i have watched you miss amory you are ambitious and your proper sphere is command <\s>
<s> you ought to shine and you never can in this house i know it <\s>
<s> i hope i shall see you in another and a happier one some day and the mistress of it <\s>
<s> the sylphide shrugged her lily shoulders with a look of scorn <\s>
<s> where is the prince and where is the palace major pendennis <\s>
<s> but there is no romance in the world now no real affection <\s>
<s> no indeed said the major with the most sentimental and simple air which he could muster <\s>
<s> not that i know anything about it said blanche casting her eyes down except what i have read in novels <\s>
<s> of course not major pendennis cried how should you my dear young lady <\s>
<s> and novels ain't true as you remark admirably and there is no romance left in the world <\s>
<s> begad i wish i was a young fellow like my nephew <\s>
<s> and what continued miss amory musing what are the men whom we see about at the balls every night dancing guardsmen penniless treasury clerks boobies <\s>
<s> if i had my brother's fortune i might have such an establishment as you promise me but with my name and with my little means what am i to look to <\s>
<s> a country parson or a barrister in a street near russell square or a captain in a dragoon regiment who will take lodgings for me and come home from the mess tipsy and smelling of smoke like sir francis clavering <\s>
<s> that is how we girls are destined to end life <\s>
<s> o major pendennis i am sick of london and of balls and of young dandies with their chin tips and of the insolent great ladies who know us one day and cut us the next and of the world altogether <\s>
<s> i should like to leave it and to go into a convent that i should <\s>
<s> i shall never find anybody to understand me <\s>
<s> and i live here as much alone in my family and in the world as if i were in a cell locked up for ever <\s>
<s> i wish there were sisters of charity here and that i could be one and catch the plague and die of it i wish to quit the world <\s>
<s> i am not very old but i am tired i have suffered so much i've been so disillusionated i'm weary i'm weary o that the angel of death would come and beckon me away <\s>
<s> this speech may be interpreted as follows <\s>

<s> she was quite mad because she could not get an invitation to lady drum's ball it was the end of the season and nobody had proposed to her she had made no sensation at all she who was so much cleverer than any girl of the year and of the young ladies forming her special circle <\s>
<s> dora who had but five thousand pounds flora who had nothing and leonora who had red hair were going to be married and nobody had come for blanche amory <\s>
<s> you judge wisely about the world and about your position my dear miss blanche the major said <\s>
<s> the prince don't marry nowadays as you say unless the princess has a doosid deal of money in the funds or is a lady of his own rank the young folks of the great families marry into the great families if they haven't fortune they have each other's shoulders to push on in the world which is pretty nearly as good a girl with your fortune can scarcely hope for a great match but a girl with your genius and your admirable tact and fine manners with a clever husband by her side may make any place for herself in the world we are grown doosid republican <\s>
<s> talent ranks with birth and wealth now begad and a clever man with a clever wife may take any place they please <\s>
<s> miss amory did not of course in the least understand what major pendennis meant perhaps she thought over circumstances in her mind and asked herself could he be a negotiator for a former suitor of hers and could he mean pen <\s>

<s> that is not the man major pendennis said <\s>
<s> he is engaged to his cousin lord gravesend's daughter good bye my dear miss amory <\s>
<s> was pen growing worldly and should a man not get the experience of the world and lay it to his account <\s>
<s> he felt for his part as he said that he was growing very old very soon <\s>
<s> how this town forms and changes us he said once to warrington <\s>
<s> each had come in from his night's amusement and pen was smoking his pipe and recounting as his habit was to his friend the observations and adventures of the evening just past <\s>
<s> how i am changed he said from the simpleton boy at fairoaks who was fit to break his heart about his first love <\s>
<s> lady mirabel had a reception to night and was as grave and collected as if she had been born a duchess and had never seen a trap door in her life <\s>
<s> and setting himself to work for what purposes will appear no doubt ulteriorly he soon had got a pretty accurate knowledge of lady clavering's affairs and fortune and of the prospects of her daughter and son <\s>
<s> the daughter was to have but a slender provision the bulk of the property was as before has been said to go to the son his father did not care for him or anybody else his mother was dotingly fond of him as the child of her latter days his sister disliked him <\s>
<s> such may be stated in round numbers to be the result of the information which major pendennis got <\s>
<s> my dear madam he would say patting the head of the boy this boy may wear a baron's coronet on his head on some future coronation if matters are but managed rightly and if sir francis clavering would but play his cards well <\s>
<s> at this the widow amory heaved a deep sigh <\s>
<s> he plays only much of his cards major i'm afraid she said <\s>
<s> the major owned that he knew as much did not disguise that he had heard of sir francis clavering's unfortunate propensity to play pitied lady clavering sincerely but spoke with such genuine sentiment and sense that her ladyship glad to find a person of experience to whom she could confide her grief and her condition talked about them pretty unreservedly to major pendennis and was eager to have his advice and consolation <\s>
<s> major pendennis became the begum's confidante and house friend and as a mother a wife and a capitalist she consulted him <\s>
<s> he gave her to understand showing at the same time a great deal of respectful sympathy that he was acquainted with some of the circumstances of her first unfortunate marriage and with even the person of her late husband whom he remembered in calcutta when she was living in seclusion with her father <\s>
<s> the poor lady with tears of shame more than of grief in her eyes told her version of her story <\s>
<s> going back a child to india after two years at a european school she had met amory and foolishly married him <\s>
<s> oh you don't know how miserable that man made me she said or what a life i passed betwixt him and my father <\s>
<s> before i saw him i had never seen a man except my father's clerks and native servants <\s>
<s> you know we didn't go into society in india on account of i know said major pendennis with a bow i was a wild romantic child my head was full of novels which i'd read at school i listened to his wild stories and adventures for he was a daring fellow and i thought he talked beautifully of those calm nights on the passage out when he used to <\s>
<s> well i married him and i was wretched from that day wretched with my father whose character you know major pendennis and i won't speak of but he wasn't a good man sir neither to my poor mother nor to me except that he left me his money nor to no one else that i ever heard of and he didn't do many kind actions in his lifetime i'm afraid <\s>
<s> and as for amory he was almost worse he was a spendthrift when my father was close he drank dreadfully and was furious when in that way <\s>
<s> he wasn't in any way a good or a faithful husband to me major pendennis and if he'd died in the gaol before this trial instead of afterwards he would have saved me a deal of shame and of unhappiness since sir <\s>
<s> lady clavering added for perhaps i should not have married at all if i had not been so anxious to change his horrid name and i have not been happy in my second husband as i suppose you know sir <\s>
<s> ah major pendennis i've got money to be sure and i'm a lady and people fancy i'm very happy but i ain't <\s>
<s> we all have our cares and griefs and troubles and many's the day that i sit down to one of my grand dinners with an aching heart and many a night do i lay awake on my fine bed a great deal more unhappy than the maid that makes for it <\s>

<s> she was quite mad because she could not get an invitation to lady drum's ball it was the end of the season and nobody had proposed to her she had made no sensation at all she who was so much cleverer than any girl of the year and of the young ladies forming her special circle <\s>
<s> dora who had but five thousand pounds flora who had nothing and leonora who had red hair were going to be married and nobody had come for blanche amory <\s>
<s> you judge wisely about the world and about your position my dear miss blanche the major said <\s>
<s> the prince don't marry nowadays as you say unless the princess has a doosid deal of money in the funds or is a lady of his own rank the young folks of the great families marry into the great families if they haven't fortune they have each other's shoulders to push on in the world which is pretty nearly as good a girl with your fortune can scarcely hope for a great match but a girl with your genius and your admirable tact and fine manners with a clever husband by her side may make any place for herself in the world we are grown doosid republican <\s>
<s> talent ranks with birth and wealth now begad and a clever man with a clever wife may take any place they please <\s>
<s> miss amory did not of course in the least understand what major pendennis meant perhaps she thought over circumstances in her mind and asked herself could he be a negotiator for a former suitor of hers and could he mean pen <\s>
<s> no it was impossible he had been civil but nothing more so she said laughing who is the clever man and when will you bring him to me major pendennis <\s>
<s> i am dying to see him <\s>
<s> at this moment a servant threw open the door and announced mr <\s>
<s> henry foker at which name and at the appearance of our friend both the lady and the gentleman burst out laughing <\s>
<s> that is not the man major pendennis said <\s>
<s> he is engaged to his cousin lord gravesend's daughter good bye my dear miss amory <\s>
<s> was pen growing worldly and should a man not get the experience of the world and lay it to his account <\s>
<s> he felt for his part as he said that he was growing very old very soon <\s>
<s> how this town forms and changes us he said once to warrington <\s>
<s> each had come in from his night's amusement and pen was smoking his pipe and recounting as his habit was to his friend the observations and adventures of the evening just past <\s>
<s> how i am changed he said from the simpleton boy at fairoaks who was fit to break his heart about his first love <\s>
<s> lady mirabel had a reception to night and was as grave and collected as if she had been born a duchess and had never seen a trap door in her life <\s>
<s> and setting himself to work for what purposes will appear no doubt ulteriorly he soon had got a pretty accurate knowledge of lady clavering's affairs and fortune and of the prospects of her daughter and son <\s>
<s> the daughter was to have but a slender provision the bulk of the property was as before has been said to go to the son his father did not care for him or anybody else his mother was dotingly fond of him as the child of her latter days his sister disliked him <\s>
<s> such may be stated in round numbers to be the result of the information which major pendennis got <\s>
<s> my dear madam he would say patting the head of the boy this boy may wear a baron's coronet on his head on some future coronation if matters are but managed rightly and if sir francis clavering would but play his cards well <\s>
<s> at this the widow amory heaved a deep sigh <\s>
<s> he plays only much of his cards major i'm afraid she said <\s>
<s> the major owned that he knew as much did not disguise that he had heard of sir francis clavering's unfortunate propensity to play pitied lady clavering sincerely but spoke with such genuine sentiment and sense that her ladyship glad to find a person of experience to whom she could confide her grief and her condition talked about them pretty unreservedly to major pendennis and was eager to have his advice and consolation <\s>
<s> major pendennis became the begum's confidante and house friend and as a mother a wife and a capitalist she consulted him <\s>
<s> he gave her to understand showing at the same time a great deal of respectful sympathy that he was acquainted with some of the circumstances of her first unfortunate marriage and with even the person of her late husband whom he remembered in calcutta when she was living in seclusion with her father <\s>
<s> the poor lady with tears of shame more than of grief in her eyes told her version of her story <\s>
<s> going back a child to india after two years at a european school she had met amory and foolishly married him <\s>
<s> oh you don't know how miserable that man made me she said or what a life i passed betwixt him and my father <\s>
<s> before i saw him i had never seen a man except my father's clerks and native servants <\s>
<s> you know we didn't go into society in india on account of i know said major pendennis with a bow i was a wild romantic child my head was full of novels which i'd read at school i listened to his wild stories and adventures for he was a daring fellow and i thought he talked beautifully of those calm nights on the passage out when he used to <\s>
<s> well i married him and i was wretched from that day wretched with my father whose character you know major pendennis and i won't speak of but he wasn't a good man sir neither to my poor mother nor to me except that he left me his money nor to no one else that i ever heard of and he didn't do many kind actions in his lifetime i'm afraid <\s>
<s> and as for amory he was almost worse he was a spendthrift when my father was close he drank dreadfully and was furious when in that way <\s>
<s> he wasn't in any way a good or a faithful husband to me major pendennis and if he'd died in the gaol before this trial instead of afterwards he would have saved me a deal of shame and of unhappiness since sir <\s>
<s> lady clavering added for perhaps i should not have married at all if i had not been so anxious to change his horrid name and i have not been happy in my second husband as i suppose you know sir <\s>
<s> ah major pendennis i've got money to be sure and i'm a lady and people fancy i'm very happy but i ain't <\s>
<s> we all have our cares and griefs and troubles and many's the day that i sit down to one of my grand dinners with an aching heart and many a night do i lay awake on my fine bed a great deal more unhappy than the maid that makes for it <\s>
<s> i'm not a happy woman major for all the world says and envies the begum her diamonds and carriages and the great company that comes to my house <\s>
<s> i'm not happy in my husband i'm not in my daughter <\s>
<s> she ain't a good girl like that dear laura bell at fairoaks <\s>
<s> she's cost me many a tear though you don't see em and she sneers at her mother because i haven't had learning and that <\s>
<s> i was brought up amongst natives till i was twelve and went back to india when i was fourteen <\s>
<s> ah major i should have been a good woman if i had had a good husband <\s>
<s> and now i must go upstairs and wipe my eyes for they're red with cryin <\s>
<s> and lady rockminster's a comin and we're goin to ave a drive in the park <\s>
<s> and when lady rockminster made her appearance there was not a trace of tears or vexation on lady clavering's face but she was full of spirits and bounced out with her blunders and talk and murdered the king's english with the utmost liveliness and good humour <\s>
<s> begad she is not such a bad woman <\s>
<s> the major thought within himself <\s>
<s> she is not refined certainly and calls apollo apoller but she has some heart and i like that sort of thing and a devilish deal of money too <\s>
<s> three stars in india stock to her name begad <\s>
<s> which that young cub is to have is he <\s>
<s> and he thought how he should like to see a little of the money transferred to miss blanche and better still one of those stars shining in the name of mr <\s>
<s> still bent upon pursuing his schemes whatsoever they might be the old negotiator took the privilege of his intimacy and age to talk in a kindly and fatherly manner to miss blanche when he found occasion to see her alone <\s>
<s> he came in so frequently at luncheon time and became so familiar with the ladies that they did not even hesitate to quarrel before him and lady clavering whose tongue was loud and temper brusque had many a battle with the sylphide in the family friend's presence <\s>
<s> blanche's wit seldom failed to have the mastery in these encounters and the keen barbs of her arrows drove her adversary discomfited away <\s>
<s> i am an old fellow the major said i have nothing to do in life <\s>
<s> i have my eyes open <\s>
<s> i keep good counsel <\s>
<s> i am the friend of both of you and if you choose to quarrel before me why i shan't tell any one <\s>
<s> but you are two good people and i intend to make it up between you <\s>
<s> i have between lots of people husbands and wives fathers and sons daughters and mammas before this <\s>
<s> i like it i've nothing else to do <\s>
<s> one day then the old diplomatist entered lady clavering's drawing room just as the latter quitted it evidently in a high state of indignation and ran past him up the stairs to her own apartments <\s>
<s> she couldn't speak to him now she said she was a great deal too angry with that that that little wicked anger choked the rest of the words or prevented their utterance until lady clavering had passed out of hearing <\s>
<s> my dear good miss amory the major said entering the drawing room i see what is happening <\s>
<s> you and mamma have been disagreeing <\s>
<s> mothers and daughters disagree in the best families <\s>
<s> it was but last week that i healed up a quarrel between lady clapperton and her daughter lady claudia <\s>
<s> lady lear and her eldest daughter have not spoken for fourteen years <\s>
<s> kinder and more worthy people than these i never knew in the whole course of my life for everybody but each other admirable <\s>
<s> but they can't live together they oughtn't to live together and i wish my dear creature with all my soul that i could see you with an establishment of your own for there is no woman in london who could conduct one better with your own establishment making your own home happy <\s>
<s> i am not very happy in this one said the sylphide and the stupidity of mamma is enough to provoke a saint <\s>
<s> precisely so you are not suited to one another <\s>
<s> your mother committed one fault in early life or was it nature my dear in your case she ought not to have educated you <\s>
<s> you ought not to have been bred up to become the refined and intellectual being you are surrounded as i own you are by those who have not your genius or your refinement <\s>
<s> your place would be to lead in the most brilliant circles not to follow and take a second place in any society <\s>
<s> i have watched you miss amory you are ambitious and your proper sphere is command <\s>
<s> you ought to shine and you never can in this house i know it <\s>
<s> i hope i shall see you in another and a happier one some day and the mistress of it <\s>
<s> the sylphide shrugged her lily shoulders with a look of scorn <\s>
<s> where is the prince and where is the palace major pendennis <\s>
<s> but there is no romance in the world now no real affection <\s>
<s> no indeed said the major with the most sentimental and simple air which he could muster <\s>
<s> not that i know anything about it said blanche casting her eyes down except what i have read in novels <\s>
<s> of course not major pendennis cried how should you my dear young lady <\s>
<s> and novels ain't true as you remark admirably and there is no romance left in the world <\s>
<s> begad i wish i was a young fellow like my nephew <\s>
<s> and what continued miss amory musing what are the men whom we see about at the balls every night dancing guardsmen penniless treasury clerks boobies <\s>
<s> if i had my brother's fortune i might have such an establishment as you promise me but with my name and with my little means what am i to look to <\s>
<s> a country parson or a barrister in a street near russell square or a captain in a dragoon regiment who will take lodgings for me and come home from the mess tipsy and smelling of smoke like sir francis clavering <\s>
<s> that is how we girls are destined to end life <\s>
<s> o major pendennis i am sick of london and of balls and of young dandies with their chin tips and of the insolent great ladies who know us one day and cut us the next and of the world altogether <\s>
<s> i should like to leave it and to go into a convent that i should <\s>
<s> i shall never find anybody to understand me <\s>
<s> and i live here as much alone in my family and in the world as if i were in a cell locked up for ever <\s>
<s> i wish there were sisters of charity here and that i could be one and catch the plague and die of it i wish to quit the world <\s>
<s> i am not very old but i am tired i have suffered so much i've been so disillusionated i'm weary i'm weary o that the angel of death would come and beckon me away <\s>
